  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5c383392-0ea5-45f0-aa9b-cf2600c58bda'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="review_759887088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759887088" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759887088?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759887088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8665535716180034353">This is the sequel to Oppell’s Airborn, which I read and loved last year. If anything, I liked Skybreaker better. Oppell does a great job capturing the spirit of “classic boy adventures” like Treasure Island and 20,000 Leagues Under the Sea (which admittedly I never read as a boy, but I caught up with later). In Skybreaker, our young hero Matt Cruse spots a ghost ship of the air, the Hyperion, and inadvertently launches a frenzied hunt for the massive treasure that is supposedly on board. The on</span>
  <span id="freeText8665535716180034353" style="display:none">This is the sequel to Oppell’s Airborn, which I read and loved last year. If anything, I liked Skybreaker better. Oppell does a great job capturing the spirit of “classic boy adventures” like Treasure Island and 20,000 Leagues Under the Sea (which admittedly I never read as a boy, but I caught up with later). In Skybreaker, our young hero Matt Cruse spots a ghost ship of the air, the Hyperion, and inadvertently launches a frenzied hunt for the massive treasure that is supposedly on board. The only problem: the Hyperion is hovering above 20,000 feet, which makes it almost impossible to reach with conventional airships. Lots of adventure, a little romance, and a good sense of humor made this a quick, exciting read. I’ve tried to “book talk” these books to my son, so far without success, because it’s difficult for me to explain the world of airships that Oppell conjures so well. Still, these books are definitely worth checking out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8665535716180034353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=its-a-boy">its-a-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=good-sized">good-sized</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107950747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10204919312593449670">OH man. I devoured this book in a few hours despite its rather large size. I was so absorbed and the pages (get ready for a pun) flew by. <br/><br/>This book continues Matt Cruses saga. When it starts, he is serving as an intern on the airship Flotsam. The Flotsam gets blown off course and as it rises to heights untraveled, it discovers a 40-yr-old mystery: the location of the Hyperion, a ghost ship legend to have riches upon riches on board. Because of some complications, the Flotsam must end it's journe</span>
  <span id="freeText10204919312593449670" style="display:none">OH man. I devoured this book in a few hours despite its rather large size. I was so absorbed and the pages (get ready for a pun) flew by. <br /><br />This book continues Matt Cruses saga. When it starts, he is serving as an intern on the airship Flotsam. The Flotsam gets blown off course and as it rises to heights untraveled, it discovers a 40-yr-old mystery: the location of the Hyperion, a ghost ship legend to have riches upon riches on board. Because of some complications, the Flotsam must end it's journey, but that doesn't mean the journey ends for Matt Cruse. With the Hyperion's coordinates and thoughts of riches in mind, Matt Cruse along with the heiress Kate de Vries and a mysterious gypsy named Nadira, set out on a perilous journey.<br /><br />I think this book maybe even better than Airborn. It was filled with the same swashbuckling action and ripping good adventure, and the romance between a certain cabin boy and young heiress grew even tenser. Now there was even a love-quadrangle of sorts with some other new characters thrown it. I think the character development was considerably better this time around, and we finally got some emotion from Mr. Cruse. <br /><br />There is just something about these books I adore. They are fun and thrilling, and there is nothing about them that makes me groan in dismay. I think that why these books get five-stars. I'm sure they could be better, but there is nothing about them that I dislike. And the visuals are awesome. I've said it once and I'll say it again: these books would be GREAT movies. <br /><br />If you know any reluctant male readers, recommend these books to them. They appeal to a wide audience. Easy enough for middle school readers, but older readers will love them too. Both boys and girls. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10204919312593449670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106834036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106834036" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106834036?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060532284" href="/book/show/3255220-skybreaker">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cara by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1879727-valerie">Valerie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106834036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12999302023579717213">Get ready ladies and gents for another adventure of epic porportions with the clever Matt Cruse and vivacious Kate de Vries. This time around we find them in Paris where Matt is attending the Airship Academy, but it isn't going as well as he had hoped. He's struggling with some of his courses and isn't living up to people's expectations. Despite that he has stumbled onto another risky endeavor. Matt has seen the legendary <i> Hyperion </i> which is believed to be a floating treasure trove. Kate has got</span>
  <span id="freeText12999302023579717213" style="display:none">Get ready ladies and gents for another adventure of epic porportions with the clever Matt Cruse and vivacious Kate de Vries. This time around we find them in Paris where Matt is attending the Airship Academy, but it isn't going as well as he had hoped. He's struggling with some of his courses and isn't living up to people's expectations. Despite that he has stumbled onto another risky endeavor. Matt has seen the legendary <i> Hyperion </i> which is believed to be a floating treasure trove. Kate has gotten into her head that they have to go see what's up there. Thrown in the mix we have the dashing Hal, the self-made man who has his eyes set on Kate, and then we have the mysterious Nadira that is holding secrets. The group sets off to set out to do what no one has been able to do, to capture the <i> Hyperion </i>, but they won't be the only ones participating in the chase...<br /><br />I was a bit worried when I started this book because I had read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/428042.Airborn__Matt_Cruse___1_" title="Airborn (Matt Cruse, #1) by Kenneth Oppel" rel="nofollow noopener">Airborn</a> a couple of years back, but the author recaps throughout the book so I didn't feel lost. This book will definitely appeal to people who love to get lost in an adventure. What makes it stand out from other books in it's genre is the concept of airships. I felt like I was actually in these ships and I could understand Matt's awe of these machines and his love for the air. In this book we get to see more of Matt's insecurities as a boy struggling to become a young man. He feels the pressure to have money, make a name for himself, and wants it so bad it hurts. He's ashamed of feeling this way, but it doesn't stop him from wanting it. <br /><br />I have to talk about Matt and Kate. Their relationship is so...<b>vibrant</b>. They click even though they are so different because they get what makes the other person tick. They do hit a rough patch here with Hal woeing Kate and Matt having an attraction to the beautiful Nadira. I did wish to see a bit more character development with Hal, but other than that I have nothing negative to say. Endings always make or break a book for me and let's just say the ending is throughly satisfying. <br /><br />The book hits all important attributes to keep readers interested, a good plot, characters that you care about and being able to immerse yourself in a new world of fantasy that is set in the air.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12999302023579717213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1883536628" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883536628" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13008769-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526002208p2/13008769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883536628?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/13008769-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781443433310" href="/book/show/21416913-skybreaker">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who likes young adult, alternative historical fiction, adventure, some romance</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883536628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3697032203426751242"><b> Skybreaker by Kenneth Oppel<br/>****4****</b><br/><br/>Matt Cruise made a name and some money for himself after the fateful trip that brought Kate de Vries into his life. Now studying at the Airship Academy Matt feels like his future is in sight. During one of the training missions however, the ship Matt is on, the <i>Flotsam</i> rises thousands of feet into the air by mishap, reaching above the clouds and showing him a glimpse of the <i>Hyperion</i> a ship of legend missing for forty years.<br/><br/>Matt returns back to the Academy to </span>
  <span id="freeText3697032203426751242" style="display:none"><b> Skybreaker by Kenneth Oppel<br />****4****</b><br /><br />Matt Cruise made a name and some money for himself after the fateful trip that brought Kate de Vries into his life. Now studying at the Airship Academy Matt feels like his future is in sight. During one of the training missions however, the ship Matt is on, the <i>Flotsam</i> rises thousands of feet into the air by mishap, reaching above the clouds and showing him a glimpse of the <i>Hyperion</i> a ship of legend missing for forty years.<br /><br />Matt returns back to the Academy to find that not only does Kate de Vries want to know the coordinates of the <i>Hyperion</i>, which only Matt know, but so do any number of unsavory beings. Teamed up with a mysterious gypsy girl, a haughty pilot only interested in making a fortune and Kate, Matt takes off on yet another daring adventure.<br /><br /><b>Skybreaker</b> was not quite as good as <b>Airborne</b> but still very enjoyable. I found the story took a little bit longer to get started and so I faltered slightly at the beginning. Once it was running though the authour kept up with his same writing technique, great story, very colourful and descriptive imagery and best of all his full and believable characters. I really like how this feels like an adventure story mixed in with science, and the character of Kate de Vries is probably still my favorite. She still has some growing up to do but her love of science and exploration reignites those feelings in myself. Great second novel, the ending had some similarities to <b>Airborn</b>, similar villains throughout but looking forward to book three, <b>Starclimber</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3697032203426751242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer148985661" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7418085648340985324">I thought this was a great sequel to "Airborn;" it was full of the exciting action and well-described characters--not to mention a most intriguing "world"--that made the first book so good. I really like how the author mixes an old-fashioned era with technology, and Matt Cruse's world is realistic and memorable. I was a little surprised by how eerie and scary (for me) some of the chapters and scenes were; I probably shouldn't have been reading those at night ;-) Not that that was a bad thing--I </span>
  <span id="freeText7418085648340985324" style="display:none">I thought this was a great sequel to "Airborn;" it was full of the exciting action and well-described characters--not to mention a most intriguing "world"--that made the first book so good. I really like how the author mixes an old-fashioned era with technology, and Matt Cruse's world is realistic and memorable. I was a little surprised by how eerie and scary (for me) some of the chapters and scenes were; I probably shouldn't have been reading those at night ;-) Not that that was a bad thing--I was just a bit surprised by it. I am definitely looking forward to more of Matt's adventures.</span>

<div id="review_84493993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84493993?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/1879727-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84493993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13263960944186799358">I nearly forgot I had read the first book which I could very well get in trouble for, seeing how many people love this series. The whole premise of historic fiction with a sci-fi twist to it is starting to have a real appeal to me now. I don't know exactly what they call it though. <br/>	<br/>Matt is just how I remembered him though he gets a bit obsessive about money, being good enough and all that. Kate is true to her character as well. Things get complicated between them, the captain, and the gypsy. I </span>
  <span id="freeText13263960944186799358" style="display:none">I nearly forgot I had read the first book which I could very well get in trouble for, seeing how many people love this series. The whole premise of historic fiction with a sci-fi twist to it is starting to have a real appeal to me now. I don't know exactly what they call it though. <br />	<br />Matt is just how I remembered him though he gets a bit obsessive about money, being good enough and all that. Kate is true to her character as well. Things get complicated between them, the captain, and the gypsy. I guess it was supposed to add to the drama. This I didn't quite enjoy but I shouldn't complain too much since it is dealt with sooner or later in the book. <br /><br />It was well written the pacing was good –not full of action all the time but definitely a good amount. The journey and discovery of the airship <i>Hyperion</i> is exciting. The action is great and I was thoroughly engrossed during those scenes in the book. <br /><br />For a sequel I think Skybreaker could stand on its own though I would recommend reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/428042.Airborn__Matt_Cruse___1_" title="Airborn (Matt Cruse, #1) by Kenneth Oppel" rel="nofollow noopener">Airborn</a> first and want to read the last for sure.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_64144272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64144272" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64144272?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who loved &quot;Airborn&quot;--and anyone who loves a grand  adventure should read &quot;Airborn&quot;!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64144272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1162109365354560221">Another great full-cast audiobook version! I very much enjoyed this worthy sequel to the excellent "Airborn" which I loved. <br/><br/>(SPOILERS FOR ANYONE WHO HAS NOT READ AIRBORN. And, if you don't want to know a thing about what happens in "Skybreaker" stop reading now and just go read the book!! It's awesome!!!)<br/><br/>The story begins with a bang as Matt Cruse finds himself in the midst of a storm while on board an airship. It was strange at first that he wasn't on the Aurora but, of course, he has joined the</span>
  <span id="freeText1162109365354560221" style="display:none">Another great full-cast audiobook version! I very much enjoyed this worthy sequel to the excellent "Airborn" which I loved. <br /><br />(SPOILERS FOR ANYONE WHO HAS NOT READ AIRBORN. And, if you don't want to know a thing about what happens in "Skybreaker" stop reading now and just go read the book!! It's awesome!!!)<br /><br />The story begins with a bang as Matt Cruse finds himself in the midst of a storm while on board an airship. It was strange at first that he wasn't on the Aurora but, of course, he has joined the Academy and is augmenting his coursework by crewing some non-passenger vessels. In the giant updraft from the storm, Matt spots an almost ghostly looking ship and realized it's the Hyperion, long-fabled to hold vast treasure, lost some forty years ago. The captain of Cruse's ship, blinded by lust for the treasure, orders the ship to climb even higher so they can lock onto the Hyperion. Matt knows this is terribly dangerous and altitude sickness begins to consume the crew. Perhaps because he has always felt he belongs to the sky, Matt is ultimately the only one among them capable of any conscious thought or action and while the captain greedily, groggily mutters "keep ascending!" Matt takes control of the ship, taking her back to Paris, saving all their lives. Whew! Quite the opening chapter!!!<br /><br />The story builds from Matt's sighting of the Hyperion. He meets up with Kate in Paris—where he attends the Airship Academy and she is going to University. Kate tells him that Grunell, the man behind the Hyperion and all its cargo, was supposedly an amazing inventor and also some sort of zoologist and that the ship is rumored to have an amazing collection of taxidermy with creatures long thought to be extinct. Kate wants to get the Hyperion for its contribution to Science. Matt is a bit preoccupied with the treasure reported to be on board–not that he longs to be a rich man for himself, but even with his reward money from the end of "Airborn" he barely has enough money to put himself through Academy and send money home for his mother and sisters to live on, let alone live comfortably. As ever, Matt's kindness and humanity radiate throughout the story! But Matt is also he only person who knows the true coordinates of the Hyperion. He also knows instinctively that the man who has come to him claiming to be a relative of Grunell is an impostor—and that point certainly drives home when Matt's life is put at risk. Now assemble the rest of the primary characters for this story. Nadera, a spunky and attractive Gypsy girl, who claims to have the key to open the vaults on the Hyperion. Matt trusts her completely, though her loyalty is often cast into doubt. And Hal, brought into the mix by Kate. He has the "skybreaker" ship that can take them to the high altitudes where they will find the Hyperion. A "self-made" man, he has plenty of courage, a bit of grit, and a gentlemanly demeanor—and he seems to have designs on Kate. <br /><br />I loved the beginning segments of the story! I loved the ending of the story, filled with one mini-adventure after another, made all the more dramatic and poignant since I'd come to care for the characters so much. I'm giving the story only four stars because I don't think it was QUITE as good as "Airborn" because the middle segment (maybe 1/4 of the book) when they are making their way to the Hyperion, seemed to drag a bit. I appreciated Matt's introspection about his deepening feelings for Kate—and his undeniable attraction to Nadera—and Hal's potential aims on Kate-the jealousy and excitement and tenderness and doubt of teenage romances brought into a pleasantly sensitive and thoughtful light. But, given the overarching "feel" of the story, I wanted a bit more excitement/action to be interspersed with the romance bits and I think much of Oppel's target audience would feel the same. However, the second half of the book more than made up for that and I was rapt, so very curious as to what would happen, all the way to the end. <br /><br />I can hardly wait for the third book in the series. It's not coming out on full cast audio until the middle of October so I may just have to read in good-old, hand-held paper form! :-)<br /><br />*Please excuse the spellings since I didn't actually see the names in print.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1162109365354560221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_44121957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44121957" />
    <a title="Jaemi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1893374-jaemi"><img alt="Jaemi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545849076p2/1893374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44121957?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaemi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaemi" href="/user/show/1893374-jaemi">Jaemi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893374-jaemi?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893374-jaemi?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893374-jaemi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1893374-jaemi?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44121957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17016003589561760273">In this sequel to Airborn, we pick up about where we left off. Matt’s taken his money and used it to enroll in the Airship Academy, sending some home for his mother and sister’s. Kate has enrolled in the Sorbonne and taken up flying lessons. The adventure begins with Matt’s internship about the Flotsam.<br/><br/>Assistant to the Navigator, he’s learning things he never really took the time to notice board the Aurora. He was always more concerned with the flying than the routes. And while he appreciates hi</span>
  <span id="freeText17016003589561760273" style="display:none">In this sequel to Airborn, we pick up about where we left off. Matt’s taken his money and used it to enroll in the Airship Academy, sending some home for his mother and sister’s. Kate has enrolled in the Sorbonne and taken up flying lessons. The adventure begins with Matt’s internship about the Flotsam.<br /><br />Assistant to the Navigator, he’s learning things he never really took the time to notice board the Aurora. He was always more concerned with the flying than the routes. And while he appreciates his realization of the importance of the Navigator to a ship, he can’t wait to be done with the Flotsam, whose captain is questionable at best. When he flies them straight into a storm, Matt is sure he’s mad. When they get through, he begins to rethink his opinion…until they get caught in an updraft, and having jettisoned their ballast, are all but powerless to stop their ascent.<br /><br />While floating at dangerous heights, they stumble upon an incredible discovery–an airship that has become myth, declared lost years ago. At 20,000 feet she floats, a ghost ship. The captain means to salvage her, but as the crew one by one all succumb to air sickness, Matt goes against orders, vents the ship’s hydrium, and saves their lives.<br /><br />Despite the manner of the discovery, the news is still magical. While he feels a deep sadness when he hears of the loss of the navigator, Matt also realizes this makes him the only person to now know the coordinates of the mythical Hyperion. He can’t wait to tell Kate. Only Kate’s already found out. The story, it seems, has been leaked. This makes the idea less appealing.<br /><br />When a meeting with a supposed member of the family of the deceased owner of the Hyperion turns bad, Matt starts to second-guess everything. Whether finding the ship was a good thing after all, whether Kate’s scheme to go after it is insanity or a worthwhile dream. An attempt on his life and the discovery of another man in Kate’s house make his mind up for him.<br /><br />And still things don’t go his way. The very ship he and his newfound partner Nadira mean to hire is the same ship Kate has already hired, its owner the very man Matt spied in her house. And yet, the ragtag crew strikes a deal. Hal has the ship, Kate has the funds, Nadira the key, Matt the coordinates.<br /><br />This adventure is even more fantastic than the last. An excellent read, highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17016003589561760273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4990416-willem-van-den-oever?shelf=kids-young-adult">kids-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4990416-willem-van-den-oever?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289041336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9362357742169201769">Kenneth Oppel’s “<i>Airborn</i>” – the first in a YA series starring Matt Cruse – was a spectacular and thoroughly enjoyable adventure novel of the classic kind. Featuring airships, pirates, journeys to exotic places and narrow escapes, Oppel took all the familiar elements from the works of Jules Verne and R.L. Stevenson and made them his own.<br/>Such a piece of work warrants a sequel and with “<i>Skybreaker</i>”, Oppel brings back all the familiar goodies.<br/><br/>This time Matt Cruse, the enigmatic dreamer, teams up onc</span>
  <span id="freeText9362357742169201769" style="display:none">Kenneth Oppel’s “<i>Airborn</i>” – the first in a YA series starring Matt Cruse – was a spectacular and thoroughly enjoyable adventure novel of the classic kind. Featuring airships, pirates, journeys to exotic places and narrow escapes, Oppel took all the familiar elements from the works of Jules Verne and R.L. Stevenson and made them his own.<br />Such a piece of work warrants a sequel and with “<i>Skybreaker</i>”, Oppel brings back all the familiar goodies.<br /><br />This time Matt Cruse, the enigmatic dreamer, teams up once again with love interest Kate de Vries to try and locate the <i>Hyperion</i> - a zeppelin which disappeared under mystifying circumstances forty years ago and was never heard or seen of again. Together with a mysterious Roma-girl and a devilish airship captain, Matt and Kate will have to rise to an altitude of over 20,000 feet in order to find the <i>Hyperion</i>. At this freezing height, aptly named Skyberia, the team will not only have to face the brutal forces of nature and deadly high-altitude life forms never before seen; they must also face a second team who has hunted the haunted airship since its disappearance.<br /><br />Those readers who enjoyed “<i>Airborn</i>” will find all the same elements and atmosphere in this thrilling follow-up. As an adventure novel, “<i>Skybreaker</i>” delivers with all the thrills and mysteries one might expect from this genre.<br />It’s only when compared to its predecessor that this book shows some shortcomings.<br /><br />What made “<i>Airborn</i>” shine, were its many surprises. As the reader, you’d start off discovering about Matt and his wonderful airship-filled world. After that, you’d fall from one surprise into the next, when crashes, pirates and exotic nature would show up when you’d least expect it.<br />“<i>Skybreaker</i>” is much more straight forward with its plot. Matt and Kate set out to find the <i>Hyperion</i> --- and do so. From the get-go you know what to expect. Which takes away some of the edge of the story.<br />Add to that the massive increase of teen angst which Matt has to suffer throughout this book and you end up with the conclusion that while “<i>Skybreaker</i>” is by no means a poor adventure book, it can’t live up to the expectations created by the far more enjoyable first part of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9362357742169201769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12041342211205212202">This series is fast becoming one of my favorites! A great deal of this has to do with the protagonist being such a wonderful, upstanding, young man who tries his hardest to do what's right, and questions himself when he falls short (even if his failings were not from his own actions).<br/> <br/>Oppel has created a new cast of supporting characters for Skybreaker and they are just as detailed and intriguing as the cast of Airborn (first book in the series). Returning to Skybreaker are certain other favorit</span>
  <span id="freeText12041342211205212202" style="display:none">This series is fast becoming one of my favorites! A great deal of this has to do with the protagonist being such a wonderful, upstanding, young man who tries his hardest to do what's right, and questions himself when he falls short (even if his failings were not from his own actions).<br /> <br />Oppel has created a new cast of supporting characters for Skybreaker and they are just as detailed and intriguing as the cast of Airborn (first book in the series). Returning to Skybreaker are certain other favorite characters from the first book, whom I now feel are like my good friends :)<br /><br />Skybreaker continues a little while after Airborn, (AIROBORN SPOILERS TO FOLLOW)<br /><br />Matt is now in the Academy and is no longer a crewman aboard the Aurora. However, when the ship he's temporarily crewing is thrown off course and by chance discovers the Hyperion - a huge ship lost decades ago, with supposedly vast treasure aboard - Matt must decide what, if anything, he's will to risk to retrieve the Hyperion, and it's treasure.<br /><br />This is a fast paced adventure full of heart and wonderful characters. While I felt a few parts towards the beginning were a little slow, the adventure definitely picks up about a third of the way through. And though I'd probably give Skybreaker four stars compared to Airborn, compared to other books it's worthy of all five stars.<br /><br />I listened to the Audiobook and am continually impressed with it's production! Kate is voiced by a different actress than in Airborn, so it took me a while to warm up to her, but after a while I felt she embodied Kate well. And the other actors are all delightful! <br /><br />Definitely, HIGHLY recommended!!!<br /> <br />****<br /><br />Review pending - but it was a GREAT book!!<br /><br />****<br /><br />Yay! I'm so pleased to be revising these characters!</span>

<div id="review_1186723325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186723325" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25808214-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484261286p2/25808214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1186723325?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/25808214-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kids, adults who like kid books etc.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1186723325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13211607544793901432">When you finish a book lickity-split, you know it's good. Kenneth's Oppel second instalment to his Matt Cruse series/trilogy was about him, Kate De Vries (and a few others) finding the elusive ship Hyperion (if only the publisher was of the same name lol), rumoured to hold great secrets and great rewards.<br/>In terms of a book, it followed quite a linear model, with a great mysterious plot, developing characters, clever plot-comebacks, and of course, romantic subplots (because who doesn't like those</span>
  <span id="freeText13211607544793901432" style="display:none">When you finish a book lickity-split, you know it's good. Kenneth's Oppel second instalment to his Matt Cruse series/trilogy was about him, Kate De Vries (and a few others) finding the elusive ship Hyperion (if only the publisher was of the same name lol), rumoured to hold great secrets and great rewards.<br />In terms of a book, it followed quite a linear model, with a great mysterious plot, developing characters, clever plot-comebacks, and of course, romantic subplots (because who doesn't like those two together?). Really, it followed the typical story model so much that really, I should've been more exasperated by how to-the-book it was, however I think that's what children/youth books need. There are too many youth books that follow silly plots, contain static characters and/or don't have good/any subplots or which just don't offer a good story. Skybreaker instead offers what a traditional book <i>should</i>offer and more. Unlike most youth books I've read, I've found Oppel's stories always offer pretty complicated plots, not to the point they are difficult to understand, but in the sense that you won't figure out the ending half way through the book. <br />In conclusion, if you love taking an easy read but aren't willing to sacrifice quality, Kenneth Oppel's Matt Cruse books are your read to read. Plus, if you happen to be interested in anything biological, aviation-related, alternate-universe/history related, design-related or mysterious, Kenneth's world will open up doors for you and your imagination. Another great read Oppel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13211607544793901432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_65496954" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65496954" />
    <a title="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you"><img alt="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436762808p2/2082345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65496954?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" href="/user/show/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you">Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=read-around">read-around</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65496954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6490837447566826665">I liked this one much better than the first. It was deeper, and the main character, Matt, actually started acting like a person rather than a one-dimensional name on a page. It focused more on the characters than the plot, and had quite a bit of romance. Matt practically spends the whole book lusting over Kate. <br/><br/>It was also good to get some new characters. Hal was complex. I had trouble figuring out what to make of him, and whethere to trust him or not, which was fine. Same goes for Nadira, who I</span>
  <span id="freeText6490837447566826665" style="display:none">I liked this one much better than the first. It was deeper, and the main character, Matt, actually started acting like a person rather than a one-dimensional name on a page. It focused more on the characters than the plot, and had quite a bit of romance. Matt practically spends the whole book lusting over Kate. <br /><br />It was also good to get some new characters. Hal was complex. I had trouble figuring out what to make of him, and whethere to trust him or not, which was fine. Same goes for Nadira, who I found to be an interesting character. I didn't see the twist coming, though after reading it I felt like an ifiot because it seemed so obvious.<br /><br />My one problem with this series remains: There isn't enough emotion. It just dusts around the edges, and there's never any real meat to the story. The characters just aren't human enough. I don't feel what they feel or connect with them, and I certainly didn't think of the book while I wasn't reading it. There's just something missing. Random, unimportant charcters tend to get killed, which is annoying and pointless. Then the main characters never really have any emotions. They just don't feel deep enough. I just feel as though nothing bad ever happens to them. I mean, they get themselves into some seriously dangerous scrapes, but always come out of them completely untouched, mentally and physically. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6490837447566826665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9956965150628693038" style="display:none"> PERSONAL RESPONSE<br /> I thought this book was really good because it has a lot of action, suspense, and the slightest touch of romance. This series has to be the best series that i have ever read because of its contents.<br /><br /> PLOT SUMMARY<br /> This book is about a boy named Matt Cruse who has seen a ship that was supposed to be destroyed but turns out to be just floating around above the clouds at 20,000 feet aimlessly and he is the only one who knows of its whereabouts. As soon as the world hears about him knowing he is being chased by all sorts of people just because he has coordinates. Anyway eventually he and Kate De Vries find a ship and crew that will help them find the ship....To Be Continued......<br /><br /> RECOMMENDATION<br /> I recommend this book to people who like books that have anything to do with airships, balloons, and anything else steampunky. This book is supposed to take place in the somewhat close future if airships weren't turned down. If you are interested in anything with action, suspense, some romance, and some fantasy type things then this series is great for you.<br /><br /> CHARACTERIZATION<br /> The characters in this book change by learning the meaning of actual love and what infinite space can hold other than just stars and other planets.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dOS+7m9yZJD3/3GJ8VPldRvBUDOJOS8lyodhqvEUX9nYB4rRbj6hO8GkQyJZl0ujEm4lAiSsbvGE5L3JcYVePg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('speSuoxWDpXGd4ZxJ2SizAvJg8RERT3eLTcy1d7KIK8edKaFjRrLPvAstNqPoAwaAmb29enQfApjVO62XlshSA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13877176022424864459">I was born in 1967 in Port Alberni, a mill town on Vancouver Island, British Columbia but spent the bulk of my childhood in Victoria, B.C. and on the opposite coast, in Halifax, Nova Scotia...At around twelve I decided I wanted to be a writer (this came after deciding I wanted to be a scientist, and then an architect). I started out writing sci-fi epics (my Star Wars phase) then went on to swords </span>
  <span id="freeText13877176022424864459" style="display:none">I was born in 1967 in Port Alberni, a mill town on Vancouver Island, British Columbia but spent the bulk of my childhood in Victoria, B.C. and on the opposite coast, in Halifax, Nova Scotia...At around twelve I decided I wanted to be a writer (this came after deciding I wanted to be a scientist, and then an architect). I started out writing sci-fi epics (my Star Wars phase) then went on to swords and sorcery tales (my Dungeons and Dragons phase) and then, during the summer holiday when I was fourteen, started on a humorous story about a boy addicted to video games (written, of course, during my video game phase). It turned out to be quite a long story, really a short novel, and I rewrote it the next summer. We had a family friend who knew Roald Dahl - one of my favourite authors - and this friend offered to show Dahl my story. I was paralysed with excitement. I never heard back from Roald Dahl directly, but he read my story, and liked it enough to pass on to his own literary agent. I got a letter from them, saying they wanted to take me on, and try to sell my story. And they did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13877176022424864459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
